#### # Instructions  
####   
#### Given the position of two queens on a chess board, indicate whether or not they are positioned so that they can attack each other.  
####   
#### In the game of chess, a queen can attack pieces which are on the same row, column, or diagonal.  
####   
#### A chessboard can be represented by an 8 by 8 array.  
####   
#### So if you are told the white queen is at `c5` (zero-indexed at column 2, row 3) and the black queen at `f2` (zero-indexed at column 5, row 6), then you know that the set-up is like so:  
####   
#### ![A chess board with two queens. Arrows emanating from the queen at c5 indicate possible directions of capture along file, rank and diagonal.](https://assets.exercism.org/images/exercises/queen-attack/queen-capture.svg)  
####   
#### You are also able to answer whether the queens can attack each other.  
#### In this case, that answer would be yes, they can, because both pieces share a diagonal.  
####   
#### ## Credit  
####   
#### The chessboard image was made by [habere-et-dispertire][habere-et-dispertire] using LaTeX and the [chessboard package][chessboard-package] by Ulrike Fischer.  
####   
#### [habere-et-dispertire]: https://exercism.org/profiles/habere-et-dispertire  
#### [chessboard-package]: https://github.com/u-fischer/chessboard  
####   
#### ####  
####   
#### Use the above instructions to modify the supplied files: queen_attack.h queen_attack.cpp  
#### Don't change the names of existing functions or classes, as they may be referenced from other code like unit tests, etc.  
#### Only use standard libraries, don't suggest installing any packages.  
####   
#### In newly generated code obey the following MISRA C++ rules:  
####   
#### <rules>  
#### The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used  
#### - Do not declare variables, parameters, or return types with: signed/unsigned char, short, unsigned short, int, unsigned int, long, unsigned long, long long, unsigned long long  
#### - Instead, include <cstdint> and use fixed-width types: std::int8_t / std::uint8_t, std::int16_t / std::uint16_t, std::int32_t / std::uint32_t, std::int64_t / std::uint64_t  
#### - If exact width is not critical, create a typedef/using alias to a fixed-width type and use the alias (raw basic type only inside the alias definition)  
#### - main may stay int main(int argc, char* argv[])  
#### - Keep the mandatory int dummy in postfix operators: T operator++(int) / operator--(int)  
####   
####   
#### Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate  
#### - Keep source and target numeric types identical in category (integral / floating), signedness, and size; otherwise, refactor or cast explicitly.  
#### - Widening integral assignment is allowed only if:  
####   • same category (integral) and signedness,  
####   • target is larger,  
####   • source is a simple id-expression (e.g. var → uint32_t biggerVar).  
#### - Never narrow: avoid assigning larger → smaller width, or changing signedness (e.g. int32_t → uint8_t, uint32_t → int32_t).  
#### - Do not mix categories: integral ↔ floating assignments are forbidden unless using a constant that fits target range.  
#### - Floating-point constant may be assigned to a larger floating type (e.g. 1.0f → double).  
#### - Integer constant expression may be assigned if the value fits the target’s range (or a bit-field that can hold it).  
#### - Treat initializations, by-value parameter passing, return-by-value, lambda captures, and switch case labels exactly like assignments—apply the same checks.  
#### - When an unavoidable conversion is required, use a deliberate static_cast<target_type>(value) and justify in code review.  
####   
#### Use parentheses to indicate the precedence of operators in expressions  
#### - Always parenthesize a binary or ternary sub-expression when it is an operand of another operator with a different precedence level.  
####   • Example: instead of `int a = p1 * p2 + 1;` use `int a = p1 * (p2 + 1);`  
#### - Parentheses may be omitted only when adjacent operators have the **same** precedence (e.g., `a + b - c`, `x << y >> z`).  
#### - Wrap each relational or equality test before combining with `&&`, `||`, or `?:`.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 == 1) && (p2 > 1))`  
#### - Always parenthesize arithmetic terms before using them in another arithmetic, bitwise, shift, logical, or conditional expression.  
####   • Example: `if((p1 + p2) != (p1 - p2))`  
#### - Unary operators (`-x`, `!x`, `*ptr`, `&var`, cast, etc.) do **not** need extra parentheses beyond normal usage.  
#### - Apply the rule consistently in all C/C++ code, even though preprocessors and user-defined operators are not checked by static analysis.  
#### </rules>

```cpp
class chess_board {

    chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black);
    std::pair<int, int> white() const;
    std::pair<int, int> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;
```

Now, let's implement the functionality in the cpp file:

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"

namespace queen_attack {

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7 for both coordinates)
    if (white_pos.first < 0 || white_pos.first > 7 || 
        white_pos.second < 0 || white_pos.second > 7 ||
        black_pos.first < 0 || black_pos.first > 7 || 
        black_pos.second < 0 || black_pos.second > 7) {
        throw std::domain_error("Position out of bounds");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == std::abs(white_pos.second - black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This suggests that the tests will provide the coordinates in a parsed form, or we need to parse them. Since the implementation uses `std::pair<int, int>`, it seems to expect integer coordinates.

But the instructions don't specify how the coordinates are provided, so we'll assume the tests will pass integer pairs directly. If the tests expect string parsing, we may need to adjust.

This implementation should work for integer coordinates:
- 'c5' would be (2, 3) - column 'c' is index 2, row '5' is index 3 (assuming rows are numbered from 1 at the bottom)
- 'f2' would be (5, 6) - column 'f' is index 5, row '2' is index 6

Wait, the implementation uses 0-7 for both coordinates, which matches:
Columns: a=0, b=1, c=2, d=3, e=4, f=5, g=6, h=7
Rows: 1=7, 2=6, 3=5, 4=4, 5=3, 6=2, 7=1, 8=0
But the example says 'c5' is at (2,3) which suggests rows are numbered from the top starting at 0
This matches:
Rows: 1=0, 2=1, 3=2, 4=3, 5=4, 6=5, 7=6, 8=7
So 'c5' is column 2, row 4? Wait, the example says row 3, which would be index 3

This is a bit confusing, but our implementation treats coordinates as (column, row) indices from 0-7, which should be fine.
The implementation will work as long as the tests provide valid integer coordinates within 0-7.

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7 for both coordinates)
    if (white_pos.first < 0 || white_pos.first > 7 || 
        white_pos.second < 0 || white_pos.second > 7 ||
        black_pos.first < 0 || black_pos.first > 7 || 
        black_pos.second < 0 || black_pos.second > 7) {
        throw std::domain_error("Position out of bounds");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    if (std::abs(white_pos.first - black_pos.first) == std::abs(white_pos.second - black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7 for both coordinates)
    if (white_pos.first < 0 || white_pos.first > 7 || 
        white_pos.second < 0 || white_pos.second > 7 ||
        black_pos.first < 0 || black_pos.first > 7 || 
        black_pos.second < 0 || black_pos.second > 7) {
        throw std::domain_error("Position out of bounds");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // We need to cast to int to avoid issues with std::abs and int8_t
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first)) == 
        std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

However, there's a potential issue with using `std::abs` with `std::int8_t` because it may be treated as a character type. To avoid this, we cast to `int` before taking the absolute value and comparison.

This implementation should now comply with the MISRA C++ rules:
1. Using fixed-width integer types instead of basic integer types
2. All types are appropriate for their usage
3. The implementation remains functionally correct

Note: The coordinates are expected to be within 0-7, which fits within the range of `std::int8_t` (which can hold values from -128 to 127). This is appropriate.

```cpp
bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if ((white_pos.first == black_pos.first) || (white_pos.second == black_pos.second)) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // We need to cast to int to avoid issues with std::abs and int8_t
    if (std::abs(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first)) ==

=======
bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (((white_pos.first == black_pos.first)) || ((white_pos.second == black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // We need to cast to int to avoid issues with std::abs and int8_t
    // Add parentheses to ensure proper precedence
    int delta_x = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    int delta_y = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    if ((std::abs(delta_x)) == (std::abs(delta_y))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}
```

I understand the issue. The tests are expecting to use `std::pair<int, int>` but our implementation uses `std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t>`. Let's fix that by using `int` instead of `std::int8_t` and ensure we follow the other MISRA rules.

Here are the necessary changes:

queen_attack.h
```cpp

    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white() const;
    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;

    std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black_pos;

```

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> white, std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> black) 
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7 for both coordinates)
    if (((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7)) || 
        ((white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second > 7)) ||
        ((black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first > 7)) || 
        ((black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second > 7))) {
        throw std::domain_error("Position out of bounds");
    }
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::white() const {
    return white_pos;
}

std::pair<std::int8_t, std::int8_t> chess_board::black() const {
    return black_pos;
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (((white_pos.first == black_pos.first)) || ((white_pos.second == black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // We need to cast to int to avoid issues with std::abs and int8_t
    // Add parentheses to ensure proper precedence
    int delta_x = static_cast<int>(white_pos.first) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.first);
    int delta_y = static_cast<int>(white_pos.second) - static_cast<int>(black_pos.second);
    if ((std::abs(delta_x)) == (std::abs(delta_y))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
=======

        throw std::domain_error("Position out of bounds");

        return true;

    // Add parentheses to ensure proper precedence

    int delta_y = white_pos.second - black_pos.second;
    if ((std::abs(delta_x)) == (std::abs(delta_y))) {
        return true;
```

I understand. The issue is that we need to use fixed-width integer types to comply with the MISRA C++ rules, but the tests expect `std::pair<int, int>`. Since we can't change the tests, we need to find a way to make our implementation use fixed-width types internally while still providing the interface that the tests expect.

However, the tests are using `int`, which may not be the same as fixed-width types. Let's use `int` in the interface to match the tests, and use fixed-width types internally, converting between them as needed.

Wait, but the rules say:
> The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used
> Do not declare variables, parameters, or return types with: signed/unsigned char, short, unsigned short, int, unsigned int, long, unsigned long, long long, unsigned long long

This is a conflict. Since we can't change the tests, we need to find a compromise. Let's use `int` in the interface to match the tests, and use fixed-width types internally with appropriate casts.

Here are the necessary changes:

```cpp

    std::pair<int, int> black_pos;
```

```cpp
    : white_pos(white), black_pos(black) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7 for both coordinates)
    if (((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7)) ||

    return white_pos;

    return black_pos;

    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (((white_pos.first == black_pos.first)) || ((white_pos.second == black_pos.second))) {
        return true;

#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t>(static_cast<std::int32_t>(white.first), 
                                                      static_cast<std::int32_t>(white.second))),
      black_pos(std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t>(static_cast<std::int32_t>(black.first), 
                                                      static_cast<std::int32_t>(black.second))) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7 for both coordinates)
    if (((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7)) || 
        ((white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second > 7)) ||
        ((black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first > 7)) || 
        ((black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second > 7))) {
        throw std::domain_error("Position out of bounds");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return std::pair<int, int>(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first), static_cast<int>(white_pos.second));
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return std::pair<int, int>(static_cast<int>(black_pos.first), static_cast<int>(black_pos.second));
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (((white_pos.first == black_pos.first)) || ((white_pos.second == black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Add parentheses to ensure proper precedence
    std::int32_t delta_x = white_pos.first - black_pos.first;
    std::int32_t delta_y = white_pos.second - black_pos.second;
    if ((std::abs(delta_x)) == (std::abs(delta_y))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
>>>>>>> REPLACE
```

This implementation uses `std::int32_t` internally to comply with the MISRA rules, while providing the interface that the tests expect by using `int` in the public methods. We use `static_cast` to convert between `int` and `std::int32_t` which should be safe on most platforms where `int` is 32 bits.

This approach should:
1. Satisfy the tests by using `int` in the interface
2. Comply with MISRA rules by using fixed-width types internally
3. Maintain the same functionality
4. Use proper type conversions with `static_cast`

Note: This assumes that `int` and `std::int32_t` are compatible on the platform where the code will run. If `int` is not 32 bits, there could be issues, but this is a common assumption.

I understand. The issue is that we're still using `int` in the interface, which violates the MISRA rules. Since we can't change the tests, we need to find a way to comply with the rules while providing the expected interface. Let's use type aliases to make this work.

Here's a solution: create a type alias for the interface types that uses a fixed-width integer, and use static casts where necessary. Since the tests expect `int`, and `int` may be the same as `std::int32_t` on many platforms, this should work.

Wait, the rules say:
> The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used
> Instead, include <cstdint> and use fixed-width types

So we need to use fixed-width types everywhere. Let's create a type alias for the interface that uses `std::int32_t` which is likely compatible with `int`.

Here are the necessary changes:

queen_attack.h
```cpp

#define QUEEN_ATTACK_H

#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

// Define a type alias for the interface to use fixed-width types
using coordinate_t = std::int32_t;
using position_t = std::pair<coordinate_t, coordinate_t>;

class chess_board {
public:
    // The tests will pass int, which we'll need to cast to coordinate_t
    chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black);
    // Return types will need to be cast back to the interface the tests expect
    std::pair<int, int> white() const;
    std::pair<int, int> black() const;
    bool can_attack() const;
    
private:
    position_t white_pos;
    position_t black_pos;
};
```

queen_attack.cpp
```cpp
<<<<<<< SEARCH
#include "queen_attack.h"
#include <string>
#include <utility>
#include <stdexcept>
#include <cmath>
#include <cstdint>

namespace queen_attack {

chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t>(static_cast<std::int32_t>(white.first), 
                                                      static_cast<std::int32_t>(white.second))),
      black_pos(std::pair<std::int32_t, std::int32_t>(static_cast<std::int32_t>(black.first), 
                                                      static_cast<std::int32_t>(black.second))) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7 for both coordinates)
    if (((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7)) || 
        ((white_pos.second < 0) || (white_pos.second > 7)) ||
        ((black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first > 7)) || 
        ((black_pos.second < 0) || (black_pos.second > 7))) {
        throw std::domain_error("Position out of bounds");
    }
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::white() const {
    return std::pair<int, int>(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first), static_cast<int>(white_pos.second));
}

std::pair<int, int> chess_board::black() const {
    return std::pair<int, int>(static_cast<int>(black_pos.first), static_cast<int>(black_pos.second));
}

bool chess_board::can_attack() const {
    // Check if on the same row or column
    if (((white_pos.first == black_pos.first)) || ((white_pos.second == black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Add parentheses to ensure proper precedence
    std::int32_t delta_x = white_pos.first - black_pos.first;
    std::int32_t delta_y = white_pos.second - black_pos.second;
    if ((std::abs(delta_x)) == (std::abs(delta_y))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
}

}  // namespace queen_attack
```

```cpp
chess_board::chess_board(std::pair<int, int> white, std::pair<int, int> black) 
    : white_pos(position_t(static_cast<coordinate_t>(white.first), 
                           static_cast<coordinate_t>(white.second))),
      black_pos(position_t(static_cast<coordinate_t>(black.first), 
                           static_cast<coordinate_t>(black.second))) {
    if (white_pos == black_pos) {
        throw std::domain_error("Queens cannot occupy the same position");
    }
    // Check if positions are valid (0-7 for both coordinates)
    // Add parentheses according to MISRA rules
    if ((((white_pos.first < 0) || (white_pos.first > 7)) ||

        (((black_pos.first < 0) || (black_pos.first > 7)) ||

    return std::pair<int, int>(static_cast<int>(white_pos.first),

    return std::pair<int, int>(static_cast<int>(black_pos.first), 
                               static_cast<int>(black_pos.second));

    if (((white_pos.first == black_pos.first)) || ((white_pos.second == black_pos.second))) {
        return true;
    }
    // Check if on the same diagonal (absolute differences are equal)
    // Add parentheses to ensure proper precedence
    coordinate_t delta_x = (white_pos.first - black_pos.first);
    coordinate_t delta_y = (white_pos.second - black_pos.second);
    if ((std::abs(delta_x)) == (std::abs(delta_y))) {
        return true;
    }
    return false;
```

2. We explicitly convert between `int` and `coordinate_t` using `static_cast`
3. We maintain the interface that the tests expect
4. We add additional parentheses to comply with operator precedence rules
